I strongly disagree with the claim that vegan leather and vegan products are inherently better for the environment or animal welfare.  Durability & Waste â€“ Vegan leather is not very durable, making it a cheap, disposable alternative. Products that wear out quickly contribute to waste and, ironically, environmental harm.  Global Supply Chain Issues â€“ Many vegan products are produced in countries with limited regulations and then exported worldwide to consumers who believe they are making ethical choices. However, the raw materials often aren't sourced locally, and since there are very few manufacturers capable of producing these products, the carbon footprint of transportation and production is substantial.  Meat Industry Growth & Health Concerns â€“ Veganism isnâ€™t reducing the demand for meat, as the industry continues to grow. Many vegan meat substitutes rely on highly processed plant proteins that our bodies are not designed to digest in the same way as animal proteins. Unlike animals with multiple stomachs designed for plant digestion, humans lack the necessary biological adaptations to efficiently break down and absorb certain plant-based proteins.  In Conclusion: As someone who rescues obligate carnivores, I find it frustrating that veganism is often promoted as a sustainable solution when, in reality, it's another trend rather than a universal answer. If you choose to follow a vegan diet, it's important to recognize the high level of processing, chemical additives, and environmental costs involved in producing vegan meat alternatives. While the actual production process may appear eco-friendly, the global transportation, limited manufacturing locations, and industrial processing create a significant carbon footprint.  Additionally, many vegan influencers who promoted strict plant-based diets have since transitioned to vegetarianism due to serious health issues, including nutritional deficiencies and brain fog. Our bodies are designed to extract nutrients from a combination of animal and plant sourcesâ€”hence why we have the teeth structure for both.  At the end of the day, highly processed foodâ€”whether vegan or notâ€”contains preservatives, emulsifiers, and excessive salt that can be just as harmful to your health as conventional processed meat. The idea that all vegan products are automatically healthier or more sustainable is misleading.

The word algae does not have a hard g.  It's Al Gee.  It's not just humans having to change our habits to adapt to new technologies that makes them difficult to initialize, but the cost.  I'm constantly seeing things like facon for instance, that don't really taste like bacon I'm sure, and cost three times as much or more than the real thing.  I'm all for saving the planet.  I have water barrels, I recycle, I ride a bike most places that I go etc...  But when you start hitting me in the wallet, that's where I have to draw the line.  I was watching a Shark Tank episode where the people were making underwear that was compostable.  When it finally wears out, you throw it in your compost heap (for the probably .01% of people that actually have a compost heap), and it biodegrades over a few months.  Oh, and it costs nearly $30 for one pair.  Really?  So your solution to a non-existent underwear problem is to make something that is 5 times more expensive, and relies on the customer having a compost pile to really make your plan work?  Now the clear solar panels?  That sounds amazing.  Replacing all my windows with solar panels makes perfect sense.  Even at a higher cost, I would eventually recoup that cost by generating my own electricity.  Unfortunately, solutions that make that much sense are few and far between.  Out of the 21 you featured here, only a few made any sense.  The tree planting drone and the clear solar panels.  2 out of 21.

Recycling plastic to clothes: I have a grounding in environmental science so I hope that my opinion here carries some weight. This is green-washing (making a product seem more environmental friendly than it is)  as these reworked plastics are a key cause of laundry based micro plastic release into water ways. Be careful when you see an anti-bacterial label on a plastic. There are chemicals used in plastic manufacturing that are also antibacterial agents. Many unethical companies use that fact to claim that the plastic is antibacterial because trace amounts of the agent are present. However, that doesn't mean that the product has effective and lasting anti-bacterial properties that would matter to you and me. It's like claiming that the plastic water bottle you put rot-gut vodka in is alcoholic because you can't ever get rid of the faint smell of engine degreaser.

In order for success, most trees are planted as a seedling or sapling, (require planting at a specified depths and spacing), not just spreading seed like you are "feeding the Chickens" wink-wink. Basically this is not remotely possible. However, even if we entertain the thought that this is possible (which it is not), you would need a whole s-tonne fleet of Full-BS-Tree-Drones to make those numbers. Have fun with that.

Fun fact, the problem with plastic roads is that they dump out about 1000x more microplastics than the leading source of microplastics... Tires. So, while they're helping visual litter, they're exponentially increasing invisible litter... Which is the whole reason visible litter is bad.   To explain further: we are not worried about water bottles in the ocean just because they'll stay there, but rather because the ocean waves will break off particles, or microplastics. Those get eaten by fish, which are eaten by birds, animals, and people. These microplastics are really the "big bad" here, so the plastic roads are actually making the problem WAY worse. (Microplastics cause cancer, genetic issues, cell damage, etc. Etc.)

The two that I donâ€™t take offense to but rather see people making a new market for without understanding the reason why the original item is there for are the vegan leather and the high powered shower head. For the vegan leather, i get why people want it. Save the cows, use something that doesnâ€™t have a brain, heart, or nervous system instead. Itâ€™s honorable. But if you try to radicate cow leather, then what happens to that? People will still eat meat. We have been for centuries. Yes, the technology is getting better to make other options available, but the skins have to go somewhere. Keep the market for vegan leather, but please donâ€™t let anyone try to make it take over the real thing. Youâ€™d be better off taking those pineapple leaves, corn husks, and other similar things and finding a way to turn them into compost for fertilizer or something. As for the high pressure showerhead. People donâ€™t understand that the water treatment and wastewater treatment facilities already have stuff like this in mind. Taking a shower doesnâ€™t waste water. People are just up in arms about bills and theyâ€™re trying to find solutions to cut costs down. By design, the wastewater treatment facility is UPSTREAM from the water treatment facility. Wastewater comes in to the plant, the water is treated accordingly with chemicals and natural solutions to get sediment and other harmful things out of the water, then it is manipulated so that the pH of the water and the purity of the water (both in macroscopic material and in chemicals in the water) are safe for the animals in the streams it will flow into. Once the wastewater goes into the river after it has been treated, it travels to the water treatment facility where they will once again treat the water from anything harmful to humans. The pH is readjusted for safe consumption and filtered many times. Once the water treatment plant is finished, they test it to make sure it is okay, send it to your home, and then test in your area to make sure it complies with government standards. If the water wouldnâ€™t be safe to cook with, they wouldnâ€™t send it to you. Then the cycle repeats after you have consumed the water and used it for whatever you need. Washing machine, shower, drinking, watering the lawn (if youâ€™re boojee like that), or whatever. So cutting down water usage in the shower doesnâ€™t make the world a better place, it just makes our wallets a little thicker.

These techs are really cool and all but we saw time and time again that this ecomodernist approach is pretty much a capitalist lie.  Unfortunately it's just a fact that the economy cannot grow and grow without end while we have finite resources. We cannot go on about our life as usual while expecting techonology to solve every problem we have. E.g. the carbon footprint of the most eco-aware 1st world countries per capita are much higher then a third word country's whos using coal plants and not caring about recycling and such, simply because the third world country is on a lower level of growth.  So while using and developing these eco-friendly technologies are really good, it's deceiving and dangerous to say that the  problems caused by mankind can be all fixed with just these without degrowth and maintaining  exponential GDP growth.

The issue with plastic roads is micro-plastic - or almost invisible plastic particles then then end up everywhere and are the reason you can find microplastic in everything (including food and our bodies). Already paint used to mark road lanes is a source of it - making the whole road plastic would drastically increase the micro plastics problem apparently. So yeah, many of these things aren't really a solution but a step towards one. By exploring options, and any problems or solutions that may come out of these options we might find a real solution.

I suspect the plastic roads was based on a much older idea. In Naperville IL I want to say about 20 years ago, the town was rebuilding old sidewalks. When the construction crews dug up the old sidewalks, they found... things. Old pots, pans, shoes, belts, and even gravestones. They were afraid they'd uncovered an old cemetery, and stopped work until they could determine what they had found. Turns out, in the 19th century, instead of using rock and gravel for the base of the sidewalks, a lot of places asked the locals to bring household detritus. Items that were too broken to use, but were too solid to be plowed into the soil. Yes, even gravestones.  (With respect to Naperville, there's a whole other story behind that. It involves a measles outbreak.) The old broken household items provided great drainage. So now a company is recycling plastic to use in the beds of roads. Yeah, such a novel idea.

Thanks for this immensely funny video, to keep the spirits high in a gloomy grey British afternoon!  Some afterthoughts. Plastic is highly successful because its prime constituent is very cheap and plentiful. Any attempt to recycle plastic will always be more expensive than making it from scratch. Some councils in continental Europe have commissioned recycling machines for plastic materials, doing automatically from sorting to melting, producing pellets for industrial use. Producing pellets with those machines costs from 10 to 100 times more than making them from crude oil, so they must sell them at a net loss. The solution to plastic recycling equate to: finding who pays for that loss. In the case of the Swiss municipality I mentioned, recycling is funded with council taxes and government contributions. Please bring back my plastic straws, thank you. The all fandango of carbon emissions from cows. The cows produce methane burps because of their diet. The addition of 5% algae to their food reduce their methane emissions to zero. The entire war against meat - targeting millions of family-run farms that produce meat, and replace them with few mega-structures producing "vegetable meat". The same protein gunk present in vegan sausages, produced by fungus in giant biological reactors, and fed with heat and sugar. The human body is designed to be fed with meat, and that vegan gunk is not a suitable replacement. For the class of gadgets that power themselves. Listen. The semi-permeable catalyst membranes that have been developed to power electric cars with hydrogen can easily be adapted to produce electricity with methanol or propane, without using platinum.  Now, imagine a nice fat D cell, that you fill with lighter gas, and produce full load electricity for 24 hours. Or a power bank you fill with methanol and it keeps your phone alive for days. These are not pipe dreams of mine; those applications of fuel cells are possible with current technology at acceptable market price.  But, if 20 W fuel cells can be built in the smartphones or other gadgets, why this millions dollar market is left untapped? I can't find an answer.  Once more, thanks for all the laughing today! Truly appreciated! Regards, Anthony

I understand the good intentions behind this video. We need hope, we need to know that there are lots of brilliant minds facing all the threats to our species and our planet using technology. All those problems need more drastic solutions, and the longer we wait, the more we and our planet will suffer the consequences.

The biggest problem with wind and solar power isn't being able to produce enough electricity, it's not being able to store it.  It also makes it much more difficult to balance the power grid.  There are all kinds of technologies being developed to try and store very large amounts of energy from pumped hydro, to spinning fly wheels to yes batteries.  But I can certainly see that office buildings could benefit from solar windows as they use most of their electricity during the day.  Maybe they could have some massive battery installation in the building to store electricity from those sunny weekends.

The solar panels on number 1 actually have a flaw. The flaw being that only the sun"light" will pass through the window and not the heat that accompanies the light because it is the infrared(which is not visible to the human eye) part of the spectrum that carries most of the heat. This will lower the temperature inside the area covered by these transparent panels, which can be a deal breaker in many cases.
